      <p>
       The
       <b>
        United States Virgin Islands
       </b>
       (
       <b>
        USVI
       </b>
       ; also called the
       <b>
        American Virgin Islands
       </b>
       ), officially the
       <b>
        Virgin Islands of the United States
       </b>
       , is a group of islands in the
       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">
        Caribbean
       </a>
       that is an
       <a href="/wiki/Insular_area" title="Insular area">
        insular area
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       located 40 miles (64 km) east of
       <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">
        Puerto Rico
       </a>
       . The islands are geographically part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Islands" title="Virgin Islands">
        Virgin Islands archipelago
       </a>
       and are located in the
       <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Islands" title="Leeward Islands">
        Leeward Islands
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">
        Lesser Antilles
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The U.S. Virgin Islands consist of the main islands of
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Croix,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Saint Croix, U.S. Virgin Islands">
        Saint Croix
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_John,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Saint John, U.S. Virgin Islands">
        Saint John
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Thomas,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Saint Thomas, U.S. Virgin Islands">
        Saint Thomas
       </a>
       , and many other surrounding
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_minor_islands_of_the_United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="List of minor islands of the United States Virgin Islands">
        minor islands
       </a>
       . The total land area of the territory is 133.73 square miles (346.36 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WorldFactbook_3-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-WorldFactbook-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The territory's capital is
       <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Amalie,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Charlotte Amalie, U.S. Virgin Islands">
        Charlotte Amalie
       </a>
       on the island of Saint Thomas.
      </p>
      <p>
       Previously known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Danish_West_Indies" title="Danish West Indies">
        Danish West Indies
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Denmark%E2%80%93Norway" title="Denmark–Norway">
        Kingdom of Denmark–Norway
       </a>
       , they were sold to the United States by
       <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">
        Denmark
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_the_Danish_West_Indies" title="Treaty of the Danish West Indies">
        Treaty of the Danish West Indies
       </a>
       of 1916. They are classified by the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
        United Nations
       </a>
       as a
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_list_of_Non-Self-Governing_Territories" title="United Nations list of Non-Self-Governing Territories">
        Non-Self-Governing Territory
       </a>
       , and are currently an
       <a href="/wiki/Unincorporated_territories_of_the_United_States" title="Unincorporated territories of the United States">
        organized, unincorporated United States territory
       </a>
       . The U.S. Virgin Islands are organized under the 1954
       <a href="/wiki/Revised_Organic_Act_of_the_Virgin_Islands" title="Revised Organic Act of the Virgin Islands">
        Revised Organic Act of the Virgin Islands
       </a>
       and have since held five constitutional conventions. The last and only proposed Constitution, adopted by the
       <a href="/wiki/Fifth_Constitutional_Convention_of_the_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Fifth Constitutional Convention of the U.S. Virgin Islands">
        Fifth Constitutional Convention of the U.S. Virgin Islands
       </a>
       in 2009, was rejected by the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">
        U.S. Congress
       </a>
       in 2010, which urged the convention to reconvene to address the concerns Congress and the
       <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Barack_Obama" title="Presidency of Barack Obama">
        Obama Administration
       </a>
       had with the proposed document. The
       <a href="/wiki/Fifth_Constitutional_Convention_of_the_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Fifth Constitutional Convention of the U.S. Virgin Islands">
        Fifth Constitutional Convention of the U.S. Virgin Islands
       </a>
       met in October 2012 to address these concerns, but was not able to produce a revised Constitution before its October 31 deadline.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2010 the population was 106,405,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and mostly
       <a href="/wiki/Afro-Caribbean" title="Afro-Caribbean">
        Afro-Caribbean
       </a>
       . Tourism and related categories are the primary economic activity, employing a high percentage of the
       <i>
        civilian
       </i>
       non-farm labor force that totaled 42,752 persons in 2016. (The total non-farm labor force was 48,278 persons.) Private sector jobs made up 71 percent of the total workforce. The average private sector salary was $34,088 and the average public sector salary was $52,572.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In a May 2016 report, some 11,000 people were categorized as being involved in some aspect of agriculture in the first half of 2016 but this category makes up a small part of the total economy. (The islands have a significant rum manufacturing sector.) At that time, there were approximately 607 manufacturing jobs and 1,487 natural resource and construction jobs. The single largest employer was the government.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In mid February 2017, the USVI was facing a financial crisis due to a very high debt level of $2 billion and a structural budget deficit of $110 million.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Baribeau_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Baribeau-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gilbert_8-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Gilbert-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

        </li>
       </ul>
      </div>
      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section
          <b>
           needs additional citations for
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            verification
           </a>
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please help
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit">
            improve this article
           </a>
           by
           <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">
            adding citations to reliable sources
           </a>
           . Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (January 2017)
           </i>
          </small>
          <small class="hide-when-compact">
           <i>
            (
            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">
             Learn how and when to remove this template message
            </a>
            )
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="History of the United States Virgin Islands">
        History of the United States Virgin Islands
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The U.S. Virgin Islands were originally inhabited by the
       <a href="/wiki/Ciboney" title="Ciboney">
        Ciboney
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" title="Island Caribs">
        Carib
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Arawak" title="Arawak">
        Arawaks
       </a>
       . The islands were named by
       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">
        Christopher Columbus
       </a>
       on his second voyage in 1493 for
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Ursula" title="Saint Ursula">
        Saint Ursula
       </a>
       and her
       <a href="/wiki/Virginity" title="Virginity">
        virgin
       </a>
       followers. Over the next two hundred years, the islands were held by many European powers, including Spain, Great Britain, the Netherlands, France, and
       <a href="/wiki/Denmark%E2%80%93Norway" title="Denmark–Norway">
        Denmark–Norway
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Danish_West_India_Company" title="Danish West India Company">
        Danish West India Company
       </a>
       settled on
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Thomas,_United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="Saint Thomas, United States Virgin Islands">
        Saint Thomas
       </a>
       in 1672, settled on
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_John,_United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="Saint John, United States Virgin Islands">
        Saint John
       </a>
       in 1694, and purchased
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Croix,_United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="Saint Croix, United States Virgin Islands">
        Saint Croix
       </a>
       from France in 1733.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The islands became royal Danish colonies in 1754, named the Danish West Indian Islands (
       <a href="/wiki/Danish_language" title="Danish language">
        Danish
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="da">
         De dansk-vestindiske øer
        </span>
       </i>
       ).
       <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">
        Sugarcane
       </a>
       , produced by
       <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">
        slave
       </a>
       labor, drove the islands'
       <a href="/wiki/Economics" title="Economics">
        economy
       </a>
       during the 18th and early 19th centuries, until the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abolition_of_slavery_timeline#1800–1849" title="Abolition of slavery timeline">
        abolition of slavery
       </a>
       by Governor
       <a href="/wiki/Peter_von_Scholten" title="Peter von Scholten">
        Peter von Scholten
       </a>
       on July 3, 1848.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Danish_West_India_Company" title="Danish West India Company">
        Danish West India and Guinea Company
       </a>
       are also credited with naming the island St. John (Danish: Sankt Jan). The Danish crown took full control of Saint John in 1754 along with St. Thomas and St. Croix. Sugarcane
       <a href="/wiki/Sugar_plantations_in_the_Caribbean" title="Sugar plantations in the Caribbean">
        plantations
       </a>
       such as the famous Annaberg Sugar Plantation were established in great numbers on St. John because of the intense heat and fertile terrain that provided ideal growing conditions. The establishment of sugarcane plantations also led to the buying of more slaves from
       <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">
        Africa
       </a>
       . In 1733, St. John was the site of one of the
       <a href="/wiki/1733_slave_insurrection_on_St._John" title="1733 slave insurrection on St. John">
        first significant slave rebellions
       </a>
       in the New World when Akwamu slaves from the Gold Coast took over the island for six months.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Danish were able to defeat the enslaved Africans with help from the French in
       <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">
        Martinique
       </a>
       . Instead of allowing themselves to be recaptured, more than a dozen of the ringleaders shot themselves before the French forces could capture them and call them to account for their activities during the period of rebel control. It is estimated that by 1775, slaves outnumbered the Danish settlers by a ratio of 5:1. The indigenous Caribs and Arawaks were also used as slave labor to the point of the entire native population being absorbed into the larger groups. Slavery was abolished in the Virgin Islands on July 3, 1848.
      </p>
      <p>
       Although some plantation owners refused to accept the abolition, some 5,000 Black people were freed while another 17,000 remained enslaved. In that era, slaves labored mainly on sugar plantations. Other crops included cotton and indigo. Over the following years, strict labor laws were implemented several times, leading planters to abandon their estates, causing a significant drop in population and the overall economy. In the late 1800s, numerous natural disasters added to worsen the situation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS">
          <span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (February 2017)">
           better source needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       For the remainder of the period of Danish rule the islands were not economically viable and significant transfers were made from the Danish state budgets to the authorities in the islands. In 1867 a treaty to sell Saint Thomas and Saint John to the United States was agreed, but the sale was never effected.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Danish_National_Archives_11-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Danish_National_Archives-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A number of reforms aimed at reviving the islands' economy were attempted, but none had great success. A second draft treaty to sell the islands to the United States was negotiated in 1902 but was defeated in the upper house of the Danish parliament in a balanced ballot (because the opposition carried a 97-year-old life member into the chamber).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Danish_National_Archives_11-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Danish_National_Archives-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FEMA_-_3094_-_Photograph_by_FEMA_News_Photo_taken_on_09-25-1995_in_US_Virgin_Islands.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1952" data-file-width="2940" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/FEMA_-_3094_-_Photograph_by_FEMA_News_Photo_taken_on_09-25-1995_in_US_Virgin_Islands.jpg/300px-FEMA_-_3094_-_Photograph_by_FEMA_News_Photo_taken_on_09-25-1995_in_US_Virgin_Islands.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/FEMA_-_3094_-_Photograph_by_FEMA_News_Photo_taken_on_09-25-1995_in_US_Virgin_Islands.jpg/450px-FEMA_-_3094_-_Photograph_by_FEMA_News_Photo_taken_on_09-25-1995_in_US_Virgin_Islands.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/FEMA_-_3094_-_Photograph_by_FEMA_News_Photo_taken_on_09-25-1995_in_US_Virgin_Islands.jpg/600px-FEMA_-_3094_-_Photograph_by_FEMA_News_Photo_taken_on_09-25-1995_in_US_Virgin_Islands.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FEMA_-_3094_-_Photograph_by_FEMA_News_Photo_taken_on_09-25-1995_in_US_Virgin_Islands.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The aftermath of
         <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Marilyn" title="Hurricane Marilyn">
          Hurricane Marilyn
         </a>
         on the island of St. Thomas, 1995.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The onset of World War I brought the reforms to a close and again left the islands isolated and exposed. During the
       <a href="/wiki/Submarine_warfare" title="Submarine warfare">
        submarine warfare
       </a>
       phases of the war, the United States, fearing that the islands might be seized by Germany as a submarine base, again approached Denmark about buying them. After a few months of negotiations, a selling price of $25 million in United States gold coin was agreed, equivalent to $562.23 million in 2017 dollars. At the same time the economics of continued possession weighed heavily on the minds of Danish decision makers, and a consensus in favor of selling emerged in the Danish parliament.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_the_Danish_West_Indies" title="Treaty of the Danish West Indies">
        Treaty of the Danish West Indies
       </a>
       was signed in August 1916,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-treaty_12-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-treaty-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       with a
       <a href="/wiki/Danish_West_Indian_Islands_sale_referendum,_1916" title="Danish West Indian Islands sale referendum, 1916">
        Danish referendum
       </a>
       held in December 1916 to confirm the decision. The deal was finalized on January 17, 1917, when the United States and Denmark exchanged their respective treaty ratifications. The United States took possession of the islands on March 31, 1917 and the territory was renamed the Virgin Islands of the United States. Every year
       <a href="/wiki/Transfer_Day" title="Transfer Day">
        Transfer Day
       </a>
       is recognized as a holiday, to commemorate the acquisition of the islands by the United States.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Transfer_Day_13-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Transfer_Day-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       U.S. citizenship was granted to the inhabitants of the islands in 1927. The U.S. dollar was adopted in the territory in 1934
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Report_of_the_Governor_of_the_Virgin_Islands_14-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Report_of_the_Governor_of_the_Virgin_Islands-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and from 1935 to 1939 the islands were a part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Customs_territory" title="Customs territory">
        United States customs area
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Statistical_Abstract_of_the_United_States_15-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Statistical_Abstract_of_the_United_States-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Water_Island,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Water Island, U.S. Virgin Islands">
        Water Island
       </a>
       , a small island to the south of St. Thomas, was initially administered by the U.S. federal government and did not become a part of the United States Virgin Islands territory until 1996, when 50 acres (20 ha) of land was transferred to the territorial government. The remaining 200 acres (81 ha) of the island were purchased from the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_the_Interior" title="United States Department of the Interior">
        United States Department of the Interior
       </a>
       in May 2005 for $10, a transaction that marked the official change in jurisdiction.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hugo" title="Hurricane Hugo">
        Hurricane Hugo
       </a>
       struck the U.S. Virgin Islands in 1989, causing catastrophic physical and economic damage, particularly on the island of St. Croix. The territory was again struck by
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Marilyn" title="Hurricane Marilyn">
        Hurricane Marilyn
       </a>
       in 1995, killing eight people and causing more than $2 billion in damage. The islands were again struck by Hurricanes
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Bertha_(1996)" title="Hurricane Bertha (1996)">
        Bertha
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Georges" title="Hurricane Georges">
        Georges
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Lenny" title="Hurricane Lenny">
        Lenny
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Omar" title="Hurricane Omar">
        Omar
       </a>
       in 1996, 1998, 1999, and 2008, respectively, but damage was not as severe in those storms. In 2017,
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">
        Hurricane Irma
       </a>
       caused catastrophic damage to St. John and St. Thomas; just days later,
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">
        Hurricane Maria
       </a>
       's eyewall crossed over St. Croix.
      </p>
      <p>
       Until February 2012, the
       <a href="/wiki/Hovensa" title="Hovensa">
        Hovensa
       </a>
       plant located on St. Croix was one of the world's largest petroleum refineries and contributed about 20% of the territory's GDP. The facility stopped exporting petroleum products in 2014. In the final year of full refinery operations, the value of exported petroleum products was $12.7 billion (2011 fiscal year).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After being shut down, it has operated as no more than an oil storage facility; the closure had provoked a local economic crisis.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="Geography of the United States Virgin Islands">
        Geography of the United States Virgin Islands
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:331px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Virgin_Islands-CIA_WFB_Map.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="353" data-file-width="329" height="353" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c5/Virgin_Islands-CIA_WFB_Map.png" width="329"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Virgin_Islands-CIA_WFB_Map.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A map of the United States Virgin Islands.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The U.S. Virgin Islands are in the Atlantic Ocean, about 40 miles (60 km) east of
       <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">
        Puerto Rico
       </a>
       and immediately west of the
       <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands" title="British Virgin Islands">
        British Virgin Islands
       </a>
       . They share the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virgin_Islands_Archipelago" title="Virgin Islands Archipelago">
        Virgin Islands Archipelago
       </a>
       with the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_Virgin_Islands" title="Puerto Rican Virgin Islands">
        Puerto Rican Virgin Islands
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Vieques,_Puerto_Rico" title="Vieques, Puerto Rico">
        Vieques
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Culebra,_Puerto_Rico" title="Culebra, Puerto Rico">
        Culebra
       </a>
       (administered by Puerto Rico), and the British Virgin Islands.
      </p>
      <p>
       The territory consists of three main islands:
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Thomas,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Saint Thomas, U.S. Virgin Islands">
        Saint Thomas
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_John,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Saint John, U.S. Virgin Islands">
        Saint John
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Croix" title="Saint Croix">
        Saint Croix
       </a>
       , as well as several
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islands_of_the_United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="Islands of the United States Virgin Islands">
        dozen smaller islands
       </a>
       . The main islands have nicknames often used by locals: "Twin City" (St. Croix), "Rock City" (St. Thomas) and "Love City" (St. John).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The combined land area of the islands is roughly twice the size of Washington, D.C.
      </p>
      <p>
       The U.S. Virgin Islands are known for their white sand beaches, including
       <a href="/wiki/Magens_Bay" title="Magens Bay">
        Magens Bay
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Trunk_Bay" title="Trunk Bay">
        Trunk Bay
       </a>
       , and strategic
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (October 2014)">
           clarification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       harbors, including
       <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Amalie,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Charlotte Amalie, U.S. Virgin Islands">
        Charlotte Amalie
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Christiansted,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Christiansted, U.S. Virgin Islands">
        Christiansted
       </a>
       . Like most Caribbean islands, the islands of the Virgin Islands, including Saint Thomas, are volcanic in origin and hilly. The highest point is
       <a href="/wiki/Crown_Mountain_(United_States_Virgin_Islands)" title="Crown Mountain (United States Virgin Islands)">
        Crown Mountain
       </a>
       , Saint Thomas (1,555 ft or 474 m).
      </p>
      <p>
       Saint Croix, the largest of the U.S. Virgin Islands, lies to the south and has a flatter terrain due to being coral in origin. The
       <a href="/wiki/National_Park_Service" title="National Park Service">
        National Park Service
       </a>
       manages more than half of Saint John, nearly all of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hassel_Island,_United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="Hassel Island, United States Virgin Islands">
        Hassel Island
       </a>
       , and many acres of
       <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">
        coral reef
       </a>
       . (
       <i>
        See also
       </i>
       <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Islands_National_Park" title="Virgin Islands National Park">
        Virgin Islands National Park
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Islands_Coral_Reef_National_Monument" title="Virgin Islands Coral Reef National Monument">
        Virgin Islands Coral Reef National Monument
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Buck_Island_Reef_National_Monument" title="Buck Island Reef National Monument">
        Buck Island Reef National Monument
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Christiansted_National_Historic_Site" title="Christiansted National Historic Site">
        Christiansted National Historic Site
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Salt_River_Bay_National_Historical_Park_and_Ecological_Preserve" title="Salt River Bay National Historical Park and Ecological Preserve">
        Salt River Bay National Historical Park and Ecological Preserve
       </a>
       .)
      </p>
      <p>
       The U.S. Virgin Islands lie on the boundary of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_American_plate" title="North American plate">
        North American plate
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Plate" title="Caribbean Plate">
        Caribbean Plate
       </a>
       . Natural hazards include
       <a href="/wiki/Earthquake" title="Earthquake">
        earthquakes
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">
        hurricanes
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Climate">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The United States Virgin Islands enjoy a
       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">
        tropical climate
       </a>
       , with little seasonal change throughout the year. Rainfall is concentrated in the high sun period (May through October), while in the winter the northeast
       <a href="/wiki/Trade_winds" title="Trade winds">
        trade winds
       </a>
       prevail. Summer and winter high temperatures differ by 5 °F (3 °C) or less on average.
      </p>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Climate_of_the_United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="Climate of the United States Virgin Islands">
        Climate of the United States Virgin Islands
       </a>
      </div>
      <table class="wikitable collapsible" style="width:auto; text-align:center; font-size:90%; line-height: 1.2em; margin:auto;">
       <tr>
        <th colspan="14">
         Climate data for Saint Thomas, Virgin Islands
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th scope="row">
         Month
        </th>
        <th scope="col">

        </th>
        <th scope="col">
         Feb
        </th>
        <th scope="col">
         Mar
        </th>
        <th scope="col">
         Apr
        </th>
        <th scope="col">
         May
        </th>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_government">
        Politics and government
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Virgin_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Politics and government">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="Politics of the United States Virgin Islands">
        Politics of the United States Virgin Islands
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Political_party_strength_in_the_United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="Political party strength in the United States Virgin Islands">
        Political party strength in the United States Virgin Islands
       </a>
      </div>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>

       </tr>
